  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5e5451a4-deff-4bd0-b9be-a195420262bc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer9251506276605279087">حالا همه‌چیز به رنگ خاکستری بنفش متمایل بود و برف شل و چسبنده‌. سرما به همه جای آدم سر می‌کشید و دنبال قلب می‌گشت. در اطرافشان کوچکترین اثری از حرکت محسوس نبود. سکونی بود که انسان را فرو می‌بلعید و مغز را که هنوز زنده بود و آنها همه در شخص دیگری می‌گذشت. دیگر نه در درون انسان اثری از کثافت‌کاری‌های روانی بود نه در بیرون. لنی کم‌کم داشت به قدری به این مسائل بی‌اعتنا می‌شد ک</span>
  <span id="freeText9251506276605279087" style="display:none">حالا همه‌چیز به رنگ خاکستری بنفش متمایل بود و برف شل و چسبنده‌. سرما به همه جای آدم سر می‌کشید و دنبال قلب می‌گشت. در اطرافشان کوچکترین اثری از حرکت محسوس نبود. سکونی بود که انسان را فرو می‌بلعید و مغز را که هنوز زنده بود و آنها همه در شخص دیگری می‌گذشت. دیگر نه در درون انسان اثری از کثافت‌کاری‌های روانی بود نه در بیرون. لنی کم‌کم داشت به قدری به این مسائل بی‌اعتنا می‌شد که حتی امکان داشت برگردد و...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6605789909623866180"><b>Adieu, Gary Cooper = The Ski Bum, Romain Gary</b><br/><br/>The Ski Bum is a novel by Lithuanian-French author Romain Gary (1914–1980). French translation was published in 1969 under the title 'Adieu Gary Cooper'. <br/><br/>The novel tells the story of Lenni, a 21-year-old boy escaping from America, his country of birth, to pursue his dreams in the Alpine mountains of Switzerland. The story is about how he faces his obstacles with his logic.<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه آگوست سال 2004میلادی<br/><br/>عنوان: خداحافظ گاری کوپر؛ نویسنده: ر</span>
  <span id="freeText6605789909623866180" style="display:none"><b>Adieu, Gary Cooper = The Ski Bum, Romain Gary</b><br /><br />The Ski Bum is a novel by Lithuanian-French author Romain Gary (1914–1980). French translation was published in 1969 under the title 'Adieu Gary Cooper'. <br /><br />The novel tells the story of Lenni, a 21-year-old boy escaping from America, his country of birth, to pursue his dreams in the Alpine mountains of Switzerland. The story is about how he faces his obstacles with his logic.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه آگوست سال 2004میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: خداحافظ گاری کوپر؛ نویسنده: رومن گاری؛ مترجم: سروش حبیبی؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، امیرکبیر، 1351؛ در 268ص؛ چاپ دوم 1355؛ چاپ سوم 1356؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، نیلوفر، 1380، در 287ص، شابک 9644481429؛ چاپ ششم 1385؛ هفتم 1386؛ در 287ص؛ چاپ هشتم 1388؛ شابک 9789644481420؛ چاپ یازدهم 1391؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان فرانسوی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: خداحافظ گاری کوپر؛ نویسنده: رومن گاری؛ مترجم: محمود بهفروزی؛ تهران، جامی، 1393؛ در 270ص؛ شابک 9786001760877؛<br /><br />گاهی یک نویسنده داستان و شخصیت‌هایش را چنان ژرف و زیبا می‌نگارد که آن کتاب اثری ماندگار در ذهن خوانشگر می‌شود؛ کتاب «خداحافظ گاری کوپر» از آن کتاب‌های جذاب است؛ که هر خوانشگری باید یک بار ه شده لذت خوانش آن را تجربه کند؛ خداحافظ گاری کوپر یکی از مشهورترین کتاب‌های «رومن گاری»، نویسنده ی فرانسوی است، که «نشر ایرکبیر» و «نشر نیلوفر» آن را در ایران منتشر کرده اند؛ این رمان با جملات زیبا و هنرمندانه‌ ی فراوان و با طنز ظریفی که دارد، خوانشگران خود را چنان به وجد آورده، که شماری «رومن گاری» را با «سلین» نویسنده‌ ی بزرگوار فرانسوی قیاس می‌کنند<br /><br />نقل از متن: «پدر و مادرش این خانه‌ ی کوهستانی را در ارتفاع دو هزاروسیصد متری برایش ساخته بودند، زیرا در این ارتفاع از تنگ نفس اثری نبود؛ اما «باگ» در این ارتفاع هم نفس راحت نمی‌کشید؛ روان‌پزشکش در «زوریخ» می‌گفت: «این از ایده ‌آلیسم او است» او حاضر نبود خود را بپذیرد؛ ضد طبیعت بود؛ اما یک ضد طبیعت نخبه؛ خلاصه‌ بدشانسی از این بدتر چه می‌خواهید؟ این خانه خیلی گران تمام شده بود؛ سنگ‌هایش را یکی‌یکی با سورتمه تا نوک کوه بالا کشیده بودند؛ به یک قلعه جنگی می‌مانست، که روی یک صخره برپا شده باشد؛ دهکده ولن هفت‌صد متر پایین‌تر از آن بود؛ ابیگ از آن‌جا پیدا بود؛ آن‌جا ابرها را زیر پای خود می‌دیدی؛ دور و بر آن از هر جای دیگری، شاید به جز هیمالیا، برف بیش‌تر بود؛ همه چیز در این خانه زیبا بود و شکوهمند.»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />نقل از متن کتاب: حالا همه‌ چیز به رنگ خاکستری بنفش متمایل و برف شل و چسبنده‌ بود؛ سرما به همه جای آدم سر می‌کشید، و دنبال قلب می‌گشت؛ در اطرافشان کوچکترین اثری از حرکت محسوس نبود.؛ سکونی بود که انسان را فرو می‌بلعید، و مغز را که هنوز زنده بود، و آنها همه در شخص دیگری می‌گذشت.؛ دیگر نه در درون انسان، اثری از کثافت‌کاری‌های روانی بود نه در بیرون.؛ «لنی» کم‌ کم داشت به قدری به این مسائل بی‌اعتنا می‌شد که حتی امکان داشت برگردد و...؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 02/09/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="6605789909623866180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3478706895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3478706895" />
    <a title="GERONIMO G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/119388821-geronimo-g"><img alt="GERONIMO G" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3478706895?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GERONIMO G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GERONIMO G" href="/user/show/119388821-geronimo-g">GERONIMO G</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/2705212-the-ski-bum">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3478706895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16056833708762695822">This was one of the first books I read after returning from the Vietnam War, in the 1960s and was trying to figure out what to do with my life. It was Romain Gary's novel that made me decide to try a ski bum's life. Looking back, I think that what attracted me to the novel and the lifestyle was its rejection and cynical view of things conventional. Now, decades later, I view the novel as an expression of the times, when young people like myself were in rebellion against the respectable. I see it</span>
  <span id="freeText16056833708762695822" style="display:none">This was one of the first books I read after returning from the Vietnam War, in the 1960s and was trying to figure out what to do with my life. It was Romain Gary's novel that made me decide to try a ski bum's life. Looking back, I think that what attracted me to the novel and the lifestyle was its rejection and cynical view of things conventional. Now, decades later, I view the novel as an expression of the times, when young people like myself were in rebellion against the respectable. I see it as being in the tradition of Maugham's, Razor's Edge, and Orwell's, Down and Out in Paris, London, or Kerouac's, On the Road and Dharma Bums, or Craddock's, Be Not Content. I don't think that The Ski Bum's a great novel, but it resonates with a part of my young life that I've never forgotten.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16056833708762695822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2027906759806862427" style="display:none">Stated out fun with the young ski bum in Switzerland having a great time skiing, casual no-strings sex, being crazy, exploring high mountains, defending himself from getting tied down by money or love. Then people died and he found God and a woman to love, despite swearing he never would settle down like everyone else, no longer wanting the (IMO rare and precious) wild freedom he once had. Major disappointment. Was not looking for THAT moral message in this book. Just stumbled upon it in a used book section anyway.</span>

<div id="review_690085605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/690085605" />
    <a title="Selman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4317928-selman"><img alt="Selman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285420904p2/4317928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/690085605?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selman" href="/user/show/4317928-selman">Selman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 3900110244645" href="/book/show/18303152-the-ski-bum">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4317928-selman?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer690085605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9448630788427341583">This was easily the best love story I've read in about the last three years, that is after Fante's "Ask the Dust".<br/> <br/>The novel had me even at the first pages and I was awestruck by the genuineness of it before I knew. Maybe it was just the right timing for me, I mean perhaps I needed to read such a book just now and here and that's why I loved it so much. I do not know. But nonetheless it felt utterly authentic and honest to the core which is more than enough for me to fall for it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rouWYb3pSO4i89b1711gTxaxHRwNHtPUhN+EEjPg1RBhUp1dBONTay602qc1JlZevAJ96NsT0YBqxiAdIdDVoQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kFKYAG3E1o8O1iAHRT+Wuov7VrRBxMhbpjx1FAw42F1fi5M81M7NCgKRLFWfRKCrIUg2QJfJyg9IJdEbHgjY7A==')})
  }

گلدان روی میز، قدری نگاه می‌کرد، و یکی دیگر برمی‌داشت. جعبه‌ای که سال‌ها با خودش کشیده وشهر به شهر برده بود؛ به قول خودش جعبه افتخارات.\nطبق آخرین تعریف‌های علم روان‌شناسی، بیماری‌های اعصاب و روان سه دسته‌اند. دسته اول کسانی‌اند که ادعا دارند مثل ادعای خدایی، یا رهبری، یا چیزی شبیه به این. این نوع بیماران هیچکس را قبول ندارند و حرف، حرف خودشان است. هیچوقت به حرفت گوش نمی‌دهند، فقط یک جواب آماده در چنته دارند، که هرچه بگویی آن را مصرف می‌کنند. اگر سر بچرخانی، دور و برت از اینجور آدم‌ها زیاد می‌بینی.\nدسته دوم افرادی هستند که پدیده‌ها را از عینک خودشان بررسی می‌کنند، پشت هرچیز یک توطئه می‌بینند. به افراد جامعه ظنین‌اند، برای هر اقدامی دچار تردید و تزلزل می‌شوند، به همین خاطر بیکاری را به هرکاری ترجیح می‌دهند. منزه‌طلب هستند و همین منزه‌طلبی دلیل اصلی بیکاری‌شان است. از دید آنها هرکس کار بکند به جایی وابسته است. مثلاً من که از قبرس آمده‌ام اینجا و دارم کار می‌کنم، با کمک سازمان سیا آمده‌ام که ببینم آنها چکار می‌کنند تا بروم گزارش کنم. بنابراین، اقدامات و حرکات دیگران را پیچیده در طرح و توطئه‌ای از پیش آماده می‌دانند و با آن برخوردهای خشن و بی‌رحمانه می‌کنند.\nو اما دسته سوم که من به آنها بیمار روان و اعصاب اطلاق نمی‌کنم، به نظر من دیوانه‌اند. دیوانه‌ها مشکل‌شان این است که به یک نقطه It is the tragic monologue of a woman speaking with the child she carries in her womb. <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText6070532434608074707\" style=\"display:none\">Published by Rizzoli in 1975, Letter to a Child Never Born was quickly translated and sold in twenty-seven countries worldwide, becoming an extraordinary success. It is the tragic monologue of a woman speaking with the child she carries in her womb. This letter confronts the burning theme of abortion, and the meaning of life, by asking difficult questions: Is it fair to impose life even if it means suffering? Would it be better not to be born at all?\nLetter to a Child Never Born touches on the real meaning of being a woman: the power to give life or not. When the book begins, the protagonist is upset after learning she is pregnant. She knows nothing about the child, except that this creature depends totally and uniquely on her own choices. The creation of another person directly within one’s own body is a very shocking thing. The sense of responsibility is huge; it is a heavy burden that gives life to endless reflections, from the origin of our existence to the shame of our selfishness. If the child could choose, would he prefer to be born, to grow up, and to suffer, or would he return to the joyful limbo from which he came? A woman’s freedom and individuality are also challenged by a newborn—should she renounce her freedom, her job, and her choice? <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer361418092666112883">Romain Gary was a Jewish-French novelist, film director, World War II aviator and diplomat. He also wrote under the pen name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6576543.Emile_Ajar' rel='nofollow noopener'>Émile Ajar</a>.<br/><br/>Born Roman Kacew (Yiddish: קצב, Russian: Кацев), Romain Gary grew up in Vilnius to a family of Lithuanian Jews. He changed his name to Romain Gary when he escaped occupied France to fight with Great Britain against Germany in WWII. His father, Arieh-Leib Kacew, ab</span>
  <span id="freeText361418092666112883" style="display:none">Romain Gary was a Jewish-French novelist, film director, World War II aviator and diplomat. He also wrote under the pen name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6576543.Emile_Ajar" rel="nofollow noopener">Émile Ajar</a>.<br /><br />Born Roman Kacew (Yiddish: קצב, Russian: Кацев), Romain Gary grew up in Vilnius to a family of Lithuanian Jews. He changed his name to Romain Gary when he escaped occupied France to fight with Great Britain against Germany in WWII. His father, Arieh-Leib Kacew, abandoned his family in 1925 and remarried. From this time Gary was raised by his mother, Nina Owczinski. When he was fourteen, he and his mother moved to Nice, France. In his books and interviews, he presented many different versions of his father's origin, parents, occupation and childhood.<br /><br />He later studied law, first in Aix-en-Provence and then in Paris. He learned to pilot an aircraft in the French Air Force in Salon-de-Provence and in Avord Air Base, near Bourges. Following the Nazi occupation of France in World War II, he fled to England and under Charles de Gaulle served with the Free French Forces in Europe and North Africa. As a pilot, he took part in over 25 successful offensives logging over 65 hours of air time.<br /><br />He was greatly decorated for his bravery in the war, receiving many medals and honours.<br /><br />After the war, he worked in the French diplomatic service and in 1945 published his first novel. He would become one of France's most popular and prolific writers, authoring more than thirty novels, essays and memoirs, some of which he wrote under the pseudonym of Émile Ajar. He also wrote one novel under the pseudonym of Fosco Sinibaldi and another as Shatan Bogat.<br /><br />In 1952, he became secretary of the French Delegation to the United Nations in New York, and later in London (in 1955).<br /><br />In 1956, he became Consul General of France in Los Angeles.<br /><br />He is the only person to win the Prix Goncourt twice. This prize for French language literature is awarded only once to an author. Gary, who had already received the prize in 1956 for Les racines du ciel, published La vie devant soi under the pseudonym of Émile Ajar in 1975. The Académie Goncourt awarded the prize to the author of this book without knowing his real identity. A period of literary intrigue followed. Gary's little cousin Paul Pavlowitch posed as the author for a time. Gary later revealed the truth in his posthumous book Vie et mort d'Émile Ajar.<br /><br />Gary's first wife was the British writer, journalist, and Vogue editor Lesley Blanch (author of The Wilder Shores of Love). They married in 1944 and divorced in 1961. From 1962 to 1970, Gary was married to the American actress Jean Seberg, with whom he had a son, Alexandre Diego Gary.<br /><br />He also co-wrote the screenplay for the motion picture, The Longest Day and co-wrote and directed the 1971 film Kill!, starring his now ex-wife Seberg.<br /><br />Suffering from depression after Seberg's 1979 suicide, Gary died of a self-inflicted gunshot wound on December 2, 1980 in Paris, France though he left a note which said specifically that his death had no relation with Seberg's suicide.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="361418092666112883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
